          <li><a href="#relationships-between-epics-and-issues" id="markdown-toc-relationships-between-epics-and-issues">Relationships between epics and issues</a> </li>
          <li><a href="#roadmap-in-epics" id="markdown-toc-roadmap-in-epics">Roadmap in epics <span class="badge-trigger ultimate"></span></a> </li>
          <li><a href="#permissions" id="markdown-toc-permissions">Permissions</a> </li>
          <li><a href="#related-topics" id="markdown-toc-related-topics">Related topics</a> </li>
         </ul> 
         <h1 id="epics">Epics <span class="badge-trigger premium"></span><a href="#epics" title="Permalink" class="anchor"></a> </h1> 
         <div class="introduced-in mb-3">
          Version history<button class="text-expander" type="button" data-toggle="collapse" data-target="#release_version_notes_1" aria-expanded="false" aria-controls="release_version_notes_1" aria-label="Version history"></button>
          <div class="introduced-in-content collapse" id="release_version_notes_1"> 
           <ul> 
            <li>Introduced in <a href="https://about.gitlab.com/pricing/">GitLab Ultimate</a> 10.2. </li>
            <li>Single-level epics <a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/issues/37081">were moved</a> to <a href="https://about.gitlab.com/pricing/">GitLab Premium</a> in 12.8. </li>
           </ul> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <p>When <a href="../../project/issues/index.html">issues</a> share a theme across projects and milestones, you can manage them by using epics. </p>
         <p>You can also create child epics, and assign start and end dates, which creates a visual roadmap for you to view progress. </p>
         <p>Use epics: </p>
         <ul> 
          <li>When your team is working on a large feature that involves multiple discussions in different issues in different projects in a <a href="../index.html">group</a>. </li>
          <li>To track when the work for the group of issues is targeted to begin and end. </li>
          <li>To discuss and collaborate on feature ideas and scope at a high level. </li>
         </ul> 
         <h2 id="relationships-between-epics-and-issues">Relationships between epics and issues<a href="#relationships-between-epics-and-issues" title="Permalink" class="anchor"></a> </h2> 
         <p>The possible relationships between epics and issues are: </p>
         <ul> 
          <li>An epic is the parent of one or more issues. </li>
          <li>An epic is the parent of one or more child epics. For details see <a href="manage_epics.html#multi-level-child-epics">Multi-level child epics</a>. </li>
         </ul> 
         <div class="mermaid">
          graph TD Parent_epic --&gt; Issue1 Parent_epic --&gt; Child_epic Child_epic --&gt; Issue2 
         </div> 
         <h2 id="roadmap-in-epics">Roadmap in epics <span class="badge-trigger ultimate"></span><a href="#roadmap-in-epics" title="Permalink" class="anchor"></a> </h2> 
         <div class="introduced-in"> 
          <p><a href="https://gitlab.com/gitlab-org/gitlab/-/issues/7327">Introduced</a> in <a href="https://about.gitlab.com/pricing/">GitLab Ultimate</a> 11.10. </p>
         </div> 
         <p>If your epic contains one or more <a href="manage_epics.html#multi-level-child-epics">child epics</a> that have a start or due date, a visual <a href="../roadmap/index.html">roadmap</a> of the child epics is listed under the parent epic. </p>
         <p><a href="img/epic_view_roadmap_v12_9.png" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><img src="img/epic_view_roadmap_v12_9.png" alt="Child epics roadmap"></a> </p>
         <h2 id="permissions">Permissions<a href="#permissions" title="Permalink" class="anchor"></a> </h2> 
         <p>If you have access to view an epic and an issue added to that epic, you can view the issue in the epics issue list. </p>
         <p>If you have access to edit an epic and an issue added to that epic, you can add the issue to or remove it from the epic. </p>
         <p>For a given group, the visibility of all projects must be the same as the group, or less restrictive. That means if you have access to a groups epic, then you already have access to its projects issues. </p>
         <p>You can also consult the <a href="../../permissions.html#group-members-permissions">group permissions table</a>. </p>
         <h2 id="related-topics">Related topics<a href="#related-topics" title="Permalink" class="anchor"></a> </h2> 
         <ul> 
          <li> <a href="manage_epics.html">Manage epics</a> and multi-level child epics. </li>
          <li> <a href="../../profile/notifications.html">Turn on notifications</a> for about epic events. </li>
          <li> <a href="../../award_emojis.html">Award an emoji</a> to an epic or its comments. </li>
          <li>Collaborate on an epic by posting comments in a <a href="../../discussions/index.html">thread</a>. </li>
          <li>Use <a href="../../project/issues/managing_issues.html#health-status">health status</a> to track your progress. </li>
         </ul> 
        </div> 
       </div> 
      </div>
